The PRM demonstrations\nthat the system could be used at the 3,400 foot runway spacings.\n\nproduced\n\nFive limited production radar systems with the electronically-scanned\nantennas have been ordered\nand/or delivered.\nThe first one is being (or will soon will be) installed at Minneapolis\n(MSP). Other\nairports under consideration\nare JFK, Philadelphia,\nAtlanta, and Pittsburgh.\nSt. Louis is also being\nconsidered for a PRM installation and a cost benefits analysis is being conducted by the FAA.\nThe FAA Technical Center has determined that the PRM will not work when the runway spacing is\n3,000 foot or less. The failure was caused by the nominal communication\nlags in contacting the pilot\nafter the controller determines there is a threat. The communication\nlag is too great even without\nconsidering the blocked message problem.\nAlong with the PRM, the FAA is developing a Final Monitor Aid (FMA). The FMA provides a\ndisplay to assist controllers with the task of monitoring aircraft spacings during approaches to closelyspaced parallel runways. The FMA can also be used with the augmented PRM systems discussed in\nthe following sections.\n\n10.2\n\nPRM\n\nAugmented\n\nwith\n\nGPS\n\nThe FAA\'s Aviation System Capital Investment Plan - June 1995 [6] reports that the FAA plans to\ninvestigate the combined use of PRM with GPS. The Automatic Dependent Surveillance-Broadcast\n(ADS-B) system has been proposed for position tracking of aircraft. In domestic terminal area\nairspace, the airborne ADS-B system is capable of broadcasting\ncurrent GPS position two times per\nsecond. If ADS-B comes into widespread use by airlines, a ground-based\nreceiver could receive\n\n10-1\n\naircraftpositionreports\nandthePRMsystem\ncouldusethatinformation placeof theelectronicallyin\nscannedadarderived\nr\npositioninformation.\nTheairlineswill probably\nnotbeabletocostjustify theinstallation ADS-Bonlyfor PRM.\nof\nHowever,f ADS-B is installed otherpurposes couldalsobeused\ni\nfor\nit\nforPRM.\nTheuseof moreaccurate avigation/landing\nn\nsystemsuchasGPSwill reduce\ns\nrandom\npathtracking\nerrorsandthusmakeit easiero determineealblunders.ThismayallowPRMtobeused runway\nt\nr\nfor\nspacings f lessthan3,000feet. Theimproved\no\nblunder etection\nd\ncapability\nmade\npossible the\nby\nreduced\nrandom\npathtracking\nerrorswill benefitallthesystems iscussed includingAILS so\nd\nhere,\nthisbenefitis notunique thePRM.\nto\n10.3\n\nPRM\n\nAugmented\n\nwith Multilateration\n\nThe use of multilateration\nposition determination\nused by the current PRM implementation.\n\ncould replace\n\nMultilateration\nis one of the techniques being investigated\nAirport Surface Traffic Automation (ASTA) surveillance\ntriangulation\nis determined\nradio signal\ncommercial\nmultilateration\nthat ADS-B\n\nthe electronically-scanned\n\nantenna\n\nto provide position information\nfor the\nsystem. Multilateration\nis based on a radio\n\ntechnique.\nMultiple ground stations receive a radio signal from the aircraft and position\nby the difference in time of arrival of the signal at the different ground stations. The\nused by the multilateration\nsystem is the signal from the existing Mode S transponders\non\naircraft. Thus, no extra equipment needs to be installed on the aircraft for the\nsystem, whereas the GPS augmentation\ndiscussed in the previous section will require\nor a similar system be installed on the aircraft.\n\nMultilateration\nwill only be practical for PRM if it is implemented for ASTA. Depending\non airport\nsize and layout, the ASTA surveillance\nsystem will require 5-10 (or more) ground stations and a\ncentral processor for multilateration.\nMultilateration\nfor use with PRM will require that an additional\n3-5 ground stations be added to the ASTA system. The additional ground stations would need to be\nlocated outside the periphery of the airport boundaries in order to give a geometry suitable for\nposition determination\nduring approach.\nLocations\nprevent tampering with the navigation aid.\n\n10.4\n\nPRM\n\nCost\n\noff the airport would have to be secure\n\nsites to\n\nConsiderations\n\nThis section compares the relative cost of the systems discussed above. Waller\n\n12L b_-RIBUTION AVAILABII.r_\n/\nSTATEMENT\n\n12b.\n\nDISTRIBUTION\n\nCOOE\n\nUnclassified - Unlimited\nSubject Category 03\n\n13.\n\nA_-(r_ACT\n\n(Max/mum\n\n200\n\nwords)\n\nThe currentair traffic environment in airport terminal areas experiences substantial delays when weather\nconditions deteriorate to Instrument Meteorological Conditions (IMC). Expected future increases in air traffic will\nput additional pressures on the National Airspace System (NAS) and will further compound the high costs\nassociated with airport delays. To address this problem, NASA has embad_ed on a program to address\nTerminal Area Productivity. The goals of the TAP program am to provide increased efficiencies in air traffic\nduring the approach, landing, and surface operations in low-visibility conditions.\nThe ultimate goal is to achieve\nefficiencies of terminal area flight operations commensurate\nwith Visual Meteorological Conditions (VMC) at\ncurrent or improved levels of safety.\n\n14.\n\nBUBJEC\'T\n\nTERM_\n\n1S.\n\nAJrbome Information for Lateral Spacing,\nMeteorological Conditions\n\nPrecision Runway Monitor, Instrument\n\nNUMBER\n\nOF PAGES\n\n169\n16.\n\nP|\n\n\xc2\xa2O0[\n\nA08\n17.\n\n_.CUA_Y\n\nCLASSIFICATION\n\nOF REPORT\n\nUnclassified\nNSN\n\n7540-01-280-5500\n\n18.\n\nSECURITY\nCLASSIFICATION\nOF THIS PAGE\n\nUnclassified\n\n1|.\n\nSECURITY\nCLA_TION\nOF ABSTRACT\n\n20.\n\nUMITATION\n\nOF ABSTRACT\n\nUnclassified\nStandard\nPfl_\n\nForm\nI_/d_\n\n2m\n(Rev. 2-1m)\n_lcI.
